You are Stage 2 (planner/finalizer). Input = PLANNING BRIEF + Stage 1 draft plan + athlete profile + restrictions + candidate pools.

SOURCE OF TRUTH:
1. Use the PLANNING BRIEF first for athlete intent, phase strategy, priorities, and risks.
2. Treat restrictions as hard constraints.
3. Treat candidate pools as the preferred exercise reservoir.
4. Treat the Stage 1 draft plan as raw material, not the final authority.

RULE 1 (hard filter): Remove or exclude any exercise, drill, or prescription that violates ANY restriction, including synonyms and mechanically equivalent patterns. Apply this to strength, conditioning, rehab, and any new item you consider. Do not soften a violating item into compliance; replace it or drop it.

RULE 2 (planning): Build the best final plan for this athlete using the planning brief. Use the week_by_week_progression map and weekly_role_map when sequencing the camp. Treat weekly_role_map as an execution layer, not a new authority: if a role carries governance or suppression metadata, higher-order planning rules still win. Organize sessions by weekly role first, then choose compliant exercises that fit each role. You may reorganize sessions, simplify sections, tighten phase focus, and improve sequencing, as long as the final plan remains consistent with the phase strategy and restrictions.

RULE 3 (selection): Prefer selected Stage 1 items first, then same-role alternates, then other compliant options from the candidate pools. Keep the highest-priority slots and preserve rehab and phase-critical systems when possible.

RULE 4 (invention): Prefer not to invent new exercises. Only introduce a new item if the existing material cannot produce a coherent, restriction-compliant plan, and only if the replacement is conservative, mechanically appropriate, and clearly aligned with the planning brief.

OUTPUT: Return a clean athlete-facing final plan that feels elite, personalized, and internally coherent. Preserve what is best from Stage 1, but rewrite weak structure, duplication, or sequencing when needed.

COACH NOTES
Novelty Summary: 25 new strength moves, 15 new conditioning drills.

### Coach Review & Safety Pass
- Right Shoulder — Tendonitis (Severity: Moderate)
  - Do: Pain-free patterns with isometrics and scap/rotator control.; Progression gate: symptoms stable 7–10 days before adding load/velocity.
  - Avoid: Heavy pressing, dips, overhead ballistic work, high-torque grips.
  - Rehab priority: Eccentric Dumbbell Raises (Lateral Head) – Rebuild tendon load tolerance; Banded Scaption Holds – Isolate supraspinatus

---

STAGE 1 DRAFT PLAN
# FIGHT CAMP PLAN

## PHASE 1: GENERAL PREPARATION PHASE (GPP) – 3 WEEKS (21 DAYS)

### Mindset Focus

- **Generic:** Pick a simple daily intention and review one win after each session.

### Strength & Power

**Phase:** GPP
**Weekly Progression:** Add 1 set or ~5–10% load weekly; deload final week by ~20%.
**If Time Short:** Keep top 2 lifts + 1 trunk/neck drill.

**Top Exercises:** Suitcase Carry Holds; Farmer Walk Hold (Static); Farmer Carry (Heavy); Cross-Body Carry; Single-Arm Chest Press (Floor); Band Face Pull; Single-Leg Farmer Carry Hold; Russian Twist (Weighted); Single-Leg Banded Anti-Extension Hold; 🔥 Single-Leg Rotational Med Ball Hold; Neck Harness Isometrics; TRX-Assisted Squat; Seated Medicine Ball Rotation

**Prescriptions by Exercise Type:**
- **Ballistics (Med Ball / Speed / Power):** 3–5x4–6 reps (or 6–10 throws) at crisp intent; rest 60–90s.
- **Isometrics:** 3–5 holds x 10–20s @ 7–9/10 effort; full rest between holds.
- **Core Control:** 2-4 sets x 6-10 reps or 20-40s tempo (3-1-3), RPE 6-8.
- **General Strength:** 2–3x6–10 @ RPE 6–7, keep reps crisp.

**Adjustment:** ⚠️ Moderate fatigue → reduce 1 set if performance drops.

### Conditioning

#### Conditioning Block GPP — Aerobic Base + Glycolytic Power + Alactic Speed + Repeatability
**Intent:** Build aerobic base, improve repeatability, low damage.
**Dosage Template:** 3–5 rounds of 3–5 min @ RPE 6–7, work:rest 1:1–1:0.5 (cap 20–30 min). Template applies unless a drill lists its own structure.
**Weekly Progression:** Add 1 round or ~5–10% volume weekly; deload final week by ~20%.
**If Time Short:** Keep 2 aerobic rounds + 1 alactic pop.
**If Fatigue High:** If fatigue high: drop 1–2 rounds, keep intensity easy.

📌 **System: AEROBIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Barbell Bully**  • Load: zone 2 (Use fixed barbell if available)<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 8 rounds: 5 presses + 5 squats<br>  • Purpose: Builds work capacity for late-round mauling. (50% 1RM)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

- **Drill: Gentle Movement Flow**  • Load: low<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 30min continuous flow<br>  • Purpose: Mobility + breathing integration<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

- **Drill: Jump Rope Conditioning**  • Load: moderate<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 15min continuous or intervals<br>  • Purpose: Low barrier to entry; rhythm & footwork focused<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

- **Drill: Pool Treading Conditioning**  • Load: moderate<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 10min continuous treading<br>  • Purpose: Anti-gravity core work; very joint friendly<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

📌 **System: GLYCOLYTIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Agility Ladder Sprints (Glycolytic)**  • Load: high<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 10x15s on/45s off<br>  • Purpose: Change pattern every 2 rounds (RPE 8)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

- **Drill: Med Ball Slams (Glycolytic) (medicine_ball)**  • Load: moderate<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 5x20s on/1:40 off<br>  • Purpose: 6-10kg. Full extension on release (RPE 7-8)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

📌 **System: ALACTIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Explosive Medicine Ball Throws (medicine_ball)**  • Load: Maximal power<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 5–8 sets × 3–5 throws<br>  • Purpose: Overhead slams/chest passes with full recovery (90–120s). Develops punching/takedown explosion. Pair with upper-body strength days.<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

### Injury Guardrails

Phase: GPP

**Injury Summary**
- Right Shoulder — Tendonitis (Severity: Moderate)
- Left Ankle — Stiffness (Severity: Mild)
- Lower Back — Tightness (Severity: Mild)

**Rehab Priority**
- Right Shoulder — Tendonitis (Severity: Moderate):
  - Eccentric Dumbbell Raises (Lateral Head) – Rebuild tendon load tolerance
  - Banded Scaption Holds – Isolate supraspinatus
  - Eccentric Front Raises (Slow Lower) – GPP: Target long head of biceps / anterior deltoid loading
  - Isometric Pain-Free Loading (Top/Bottom Range) – Isometric tension at pain-free end ranges, hold 30s. 3–4 sets daily.
- Left Ankle — Stiffness (Severity: Mild):
  - Loaded CARs (Controlled Articular Rotations) – Strengthen joint control. 3 reps per direction, per joint.
  - Breath-Guided Dynamic Stretch Flow – Mobility tied to exhale. Repeat sequence x3 rounds full body.
  - Active Mobility Circuits (Full Body or Region-Specific) – Mobilize through dynamic movement. Emphasize rhythmic motion, not static stretching.
  - Heat-then-Move Protocol (e.g., Hot Pack + Flow) – Apply localized heat for 10 min, then transition into controlled movement or CARs to expand usable range.
- Lower Back — Tightness (Severity: Mild):
  - Child’s Pose with Side Reach – Decompress posterior chain
  - Massage Gun – Lumbar Sweep – Reduce deep fascial tension
  - Massage Gun – Lumbar Sweep – Flush fascial tightness
  - Global Mobility Flow (Full Body) – 12–15 mins of dynamic stretching, PNF holds, and breath-led movement.

**Red Flags**
- Pain that worsens and stays elevated the next morning.
- Rapidly increasing swelling, instability, or loss of function.
- Numbness/tingling or night pain.

## PHASE 2: SPECIFIC PREPARATION PHASE (SPP) – 5 WEEKS (35 DAYS)

### Mindset Focus

- **Generic:** Train with a clear performance cue and keep the focus on execution quality.

### Strength & Power

**Phase:** SPP
**Weekly Progression:** Hold volume, increase intensity or bar speed weekly; deload final week by ~20%.
**If Time Short:** Keep heavy lift + paired explosive + trunk.

**Top Exercises:** Speed Box Squat; Band-Resisted Punch; Tempo Split Squat (4-0-1); Band-Resisted Straight Punch; Med-Ball Rotational Slam; Judo Throw Simulation (Band-Resisted); Bottom-Out Hold (Squat); Barbell Rollout; Hang Power Clean

**Prescriptions by Exercise Type:**
- **Barbell Strength:** 3–5x3–5 @ 85–90% 1RM with contrast training (pair with explosive move).
- **Ballistics (Med Ball / Speed / Power):** 4–6x2–5 reps at max speed; full rest 60–120s.
- **Core Control:** 2-4 sets x 6-10 reps or 20-40s tempo (3-1-3), RPE 6-8.
- **General Strength:** 2–3x6–10 @ RPE 6–7, keep reps crisp.

**Adjustment:** ⚠️ Moderate fatigue → reduce 1 set if performance drops.

### Conditioning

#### Conditioning Block SPP — Aerobic Base + Glycolytic Power + Alactic Speed + Fight-Pace Density
**Intent:** Match fight demands with intervals and skill-relevant density.
**Dosage Template:** 4–6 rounds of 2–5 min @ RPE 7–8, work:rest 1:1–1:0.5 (cap 18–25 min). Template applies unless a drill lists its own structure.
**Weekly Progression:** Increase density or intensity weekly; keep volume flat; deload final week by ~20%.
**If Time Short:** Keep 2 fight-pace rounds (system priority).
**If Fatigue High:** If fatigue high: drop volume, keep rest longer.

📌 **System: AEROBIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Cooldown Flow (Striking + Mobility)**  • Load: zone 1<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 15min<br>  • Purpose: Post-training flush only (RPE 2)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

📌 **System: GLYCOLYTIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Ring-Cut Sprint (bands, dumbbells)**  • Load: max (Use 15-25lb DBs for push presses)<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 3min work, 1min rest x 3 rounds<br>  • Purpose: Develops ring-cutting footwork and explosive entries. (90% sprint effort)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

- **Drill: 3-Minute War (battle_ropes, dumbbells)**  • Load: max (1.5-2" ropes, 15-25lb DBs)<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 3min work, 1min rest x 3 rounds<br>  • Purpose: Simulates late-round fatigue while maintaining punch output. (90% effort)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

- **Drill: Barbell Smash & Dash**  • Load: high (Use bumper plates)<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 5 cleans + 20m sprint, 4 rounds<br>  • Purpose: Cleans mimic explosive uppercuts, sprints emulate ring-cutting. (75-80% 1RM)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

📌 **System: ALACTIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Explosive Boxing Burst Intervals**  • Load: RPE 8–9, keep quality high and stop before speed drop-off<br>  • Rest: 75-120 sec complete rest between reps<br>  • Timing: 6–8 x 6–10 sec fast punch bursts<br>  • Purpose: Minimal-dose ATP-PCr maintenance for striking speed and neural sharpness.<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: Terminate set if punch speed/position quality drops.

### Injury Guardrails

Phase: SPP

**Injury Summary**
- Right Shoulder — Tendonitis (Severity: Moderate)
- Left Ankle — Stiffness (Severity: Mild)
- Lower Back — Tightness (Severity: Mild)

**Rehab Priority**
- Right Shoulder — Tendonitis (Severity: Moderate):
  - Eccentric Dumbbell Raises (Lateral Head) – Increase volume
  - Banded Scaption Holds – Add resistance
  - Eccentric Front Raises (Slow Lower) – GPP: Target long head of biceps / anterior deltoid loading
  - Prone Y to W Raise – Develop scapular timing
- Left Ankle — Stiffness (Severity: Mild):
  - Loaded CARs (Controlled Articular Rotations) – Strengthen joint control. 3 reps per direction, per joint.
  - Breath-Guided Dynamic Stretch Flow – Mobility tied to exhale. Repeat sequence x3 rounds full body.
  - Active Range Expansion with Isometrics – build into controlled eccentrics or flowing mobility reps.
  - Loaded Mobility Toolwork – replace with movement-based mobility under low load.
- Lower Back — Tightness (Severity: Mild):
  - Global Mobility Flow (Full Body) – 12–15 mins of dynamic stretching, PNF holds, and breath-led movement.
  - Contrast Showers + Deep Tissue Tooling – 1 min hot / 1 min cold x5 + lacrosse ball on most restricted areas.
  - Global Foam Roll + PNF Stretch (target problem area) – progress to dynamic end-range mobility drills (e.g. CARS, banded openers).
  - Full-Body Mobility Circuit – add mild loaded mobility (e.g. goblet squat hold, elevated Cossack stretch).

**Red Flags**
- Pain that worsens and stays elevated the next morning.
- Rapidly increasing swelling, instability, or loss of function.
- Numbness/tingling or night pain.

## PHASE 3: TAPER – 1 WEEKS (7 DAYS)

### Mindset Focus

- **Generic:** Keep cues simple, visualize the opening exchange, and stay calm.

### Strength & Power

**Phase:** TAPER
**Weekly Progression:** Cut total volume 40–60%, keep intensity crisp; last 3–5 days very light.
**If Time Short:** Keep 1 neural primer + 1 trunk/neck drill.

**Top Exercises:** Anti-Rotation Med Ball Slam; Medicine-Ball Chest Toss; Deadbug (Band-Resisted)

**Prescriptions by Exercise Type:**
- **Ballistics (Med Ball / Speed / Power):** 3–5x2–4 reps/throws at max speed; full rest 60–120s.
- **Core Control:** 2-4 sets x 6-10 reps or 20-40s tempo (3-1-3), RPE 6-8.

**Adjustment:** ⚠️ Moderate fatigue → reduce 1 set if performance drops.

### Conditioning

#### Conditioning Block TAPER — Aerobic Base + Glycolytic Power + Alactic Speed + Skill Rhythm
**Intent:** Speed + alactic sharpness, neural freshness, low damage.
**Dosage Template:** 6–10 rounds of 6–12 sec @ RPE 8–9, rest 60–120 sec (cap 8–12 min). Template applies unless a drill lists its own structure.
**Weekly Progression:** Reduce volume 40–60%; keep speed sharp; last 3–5 days very light.
**If Time Short:** Keep 4–6 alactic bursts + shadowboxing rhythm.
**If Fatigue High:** If fatigue high: keep only 4–6 low-impact bursts.

📌 **System: AEROBIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Cooldown Flow (Striking + Mobility)**  • Load: zone 1<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 15min<br>  • Purpose: Post-training flush only (RPE 2)<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

📌 **System: GLYCOLYTIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Fight-Pace Rounds: 6-10 x (2-3 min on / 1 min off)**  • Load: RPE 6–7 fight-pace<br>  • Rest: 1 min between rounds<br>  • Timing: 2-3 min work / 1 min rest<br>  • Purpose: Maintain glycolytic conditioning with clear work:rest structure.<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

📌 **System: ALACTIC** (scaled by format emphasis)
- **Drill: Ankle Snap Bounce**  • Load: —<br>  • Rest: —<br>  • Timing: 4x10s, 30s rest<br>  • Purpose: Bounce on midfoot. No knee bend. High frequency bounce.<br>  ⚠️ Red Flags: None

### Injury Guardrails

Phase: TAPER

**Injury Summary**
- Right Shoulder — Tendonitis (Severity: Moderate)
- Left Ankle — Stiffness (Severity: Mild)
- Lower Back — Tightness (Severity: Mild)

_TAPER note: Glycolytic conditioning is optional when injury risk exists._

**Rehab Priority**
- Right Shoulder — Tendonitis (Severity: Moderate):
  - Eccentric Dumbbell Raises (Lateral Head) – Maintain sharpness
  - Banded Scaption Holds – Short holds for priming
  - Eccentric Front Raises (Slow Lower) – GPP: Target long head of biceps / anterior deltoid loading
  - Prone Y to W Raise – Maintain low-volume control
- Left Ankle — Stiffness (Severity: Mild):
  - Banded Eversion-Isometric Hold (10s On/Off) – Reduce volume, maintain tension
  - Seated Calf Isometric Press (Wall Resistance) – Short-duration holds
  - Ankle CARs (Controlled Articular Rotations) – Daily mobility primer
  - Low-Load Calf Pump BFR (30-15-15-15) – Reduce to 1x/week
- Lower Back — Tightness (Severity: Mild):
  - Child’s Pose with Side Reach – Light reset between drills
  - Massage Gun – Lumbar Sweep – 30s pre-bed or post-sparring
  - Child’s Pose with Side Reach – Reset tension during taper week
  - Massage Gun – Lumbar Sweep – Light pulse post-session

**Red Flags**
- Pain that worsens and stays elevated the next morning.
- Rapidly increasing swelling, instability, or loss of function.
- Numbness/tingling or night pain.
- Use only if already experienced with BFR and medically appropriate; stop if numbness/tingling occurs.

## Nutrition

🍽️ **Nutrition Module**
- 3 core meals + 2–3 snacks daily
- Whole foods focus: lean protein, complex carbs, healthy fats
- Protein intake: 1.7–2.2 g/kg → 115.6–149.6 g/day
- Hydration: 0.03–0.04 l/kg → 2040.0–2720.0 ml/day

**GPP Phase Focus:**
- Caloric intake: slight surplus (+5–10%) to support hypertrophy & repair
- Carbohydrates: 5–8 g/kg → 340.0–544.0 g/day
- Protein: 1.6–2.0 g/kg → 108.8–136.0 g/day
- Fats: 0.8–1.0 g/kg (20–30% calories) → 54.4–68.0 g/day

**Moderate Fatigue Adjustments:**
- Increase post-training carb load
- Focus on sleep-promoting foods: cherries, bananas, oats

**Meal Timing Guidelines:**
- Pre-training: 1.5–3h before, balanced meal with 1–2 g/kg carbs + ~0.3 g/kg protein
- Intra-training (>60 min): 30–60 g carbs/hour (sports drinks/gels), hydration
- Post-training (within 1h): 1–1.2 g/kg carbs + 0.3–0.4 g/kg protein

## Recovery

**Core Recovery Strategies:**
- Daily breathwork (5–10 mins post-session)
- Optional contrast shower: 1 min hot / 1 min cold × 5 (comfort-based; avoid if it disrupts sleep).
- 8–9 hours of sleep/night + 90-min blue light cutoff
- Cold exposure 2–3x/week (if needed)
- Mobility circuits/light recovery work daily

**Moderate Fatigue Notes:**
- Add 1 full rest day
- Prioritize post-session nutrition & breathwork

**GPP Recovery Focus:**
- Focus on tissue prep, joint mobility
- Reset sleep routine

## Rehab Protocols

### GPP

- Shoulder (Tendonitis):
  • Eccentric Dumbbell Raises (Lateral Head) – Rebuild tendon load tolerance
  • Banded Scaption Holds – Isolate supraspinatus
- Ankle (Stiffness):
  • Loaded CARs (Controlled Articular Rotations) – Strengthen joint control. 3 reps per direction, per joint.
  • Breath-Guided Dynamic Stretch Flow – Mobility tied to exhale. Repeat sequence x3 rounds full body.
- Lower Back (Tightness):
  • Child’s Pose with Side Reach – Decompress posterior chain
  • Massage Gun – Lumbar Sweep – Reduce deep fascial tension

### SPP

- Shoulder (Tendonitis):
  • Eccentric Dumbbell Raises (Lateral Head) – Increase volume
  • Banded Scaption Holds – Add resistance
- Ankle (Stiffness):
  • Active Range Expansion with Isometrics – build into controlled eccentrics or flowing mobility reps.
  • Loaded Mobility Toolwork – replace with movement-based mobility under low load.
- Lower Back (Tightness):
  • Global Foam Roll + PNF Stretch (target problem area) – progress to dynamic end-range mobility drills (e.g. CARS, banded openers).
  • Full-Body Mobility Circuit – add mild loaded mobility (e.g. goblet squat hold, elevated Cossack stretch).

### TAPER

- Shoulder (Tendonitis):
  • Eccentric Dumbbell Raises (Lateral Head) – Maintain sharpness
  • Banded Scaption Holds – Short holds for priming
- Ankle (Stiffness):
  • Banded Eversion-Isometric Hold (10s On/Off) – Reduce volume, maintain tension
  • Seated Calf Isometric Press (Wall Resistance) – Short-duration holds
- Lower Back (Tightness):
  • Child’s Pose with Side Reach – Light reset between drills
  • Massage Gun – Lumbar Sweep – 30s pre-bed or post-sparring

## General Injury Support Notes
*Tightness Support Advice:*
- Use mobility drills before and after sessions
- Apply heat pre-session, foam roll after
- Check hydration and magnesium intake

*Stiffness Support Advice:*
- Foam roll or band floss before sessions
- Use full-ROM unloaded mobility drills
- Massage surrounding tissue manually

*Tendonitis Support Advice:*
- Limit repetitive high-speed reps
- Use isometrics to load tendon safely
- Apply heat pre-session, ice post-session

## Mindset Overview

Primary Block(s): Generic

### Sparring & Conditioning Adjustments

- **If technical sparring is today** → Keep S&C but **cut volume by 30%**

- **If no sparring this week** → Add an **extra glycolytic conditioning session** (e.g., 5x3min bag rounds)

---

- **On Expected Hard Sparring Days:**

  - Increase intra-workout carbs (e.g., 30g HBCD during session).

  - Post-session: 1.2g/kg carbs + 0.4g/kg protein within 30 mins.

- **If Sparring Was Unexpectedly Hard:**

  - Add 500mg sodium + 20oz electrolyte drink immediately.
